## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by restoring forces (functions of x), damping/driving forces (functions of v), and possibly explicit time-dependent driving forces. Classical nonlinear oscillator equations (Duffing, van der Pol, Mathieu, etc.) provide the structural templates.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Parametric oscillator (Mathieu): dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubed damping)
- General polynomial oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (quadratic + cubic restoring)
- Mixed coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**2 (position-velocity coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial terms in x for symmetric potentials
- Even-power terms in x (x², x⁴) break oscillation symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to x²·v or v³ indicate nonlinear (amplitude-dependent) damping or self-excitation
- Explicit sinusoidal time dependence sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) indicates externally driven oscillators with periodic forcing
- Product terms like x·cos(c·t) indicate parametric excitation where the effective stiffness is modulated in time
- If acceleration depends only on x (not v or t), the system is conservative with a potential energy function derivable by integration
- Linear v terms represent viscous damping (negative coefficient) or energy injection (positive coefficient)
- The absence of explicit time dependence (t) indicates an autonomous dynamical system where phase-space analysis applies
- Rational terms like x/(1 + c·x²) can represent bounded restoring forces that saturate at large displacements

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0586*v³ - 0.7167*v - 0.3583*v*exp(-|v|) + 0.6686*sin(t)`

The GT has these key structural components:
1. A `v³` term
2. A `v` term (linear in v)
3. A `v*exp(-|v|)` term
4. A `sin(t)` term

Note: No dependence on `x`, no `cos(t)` (though `sin(t)` can be written as `cos(t - π/2)`), and the critical non-standard term is `v*exp(-|v|)`.

Let me check candidates systematically.

**Key observations:**
- Most candidates have `cos(t)` instead of `sin(t)`, but `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2)`, so a standalone `cos(t)` term with a free coefficient can only produce `c*cos(t)`, not `c*sin(t)`. These are NOT equivalent since `sin(t) ≠ c*cos(t)` for all t.
- However, candidates with `sin(c*t + c)` could match `sin(t)` by setting appropriate phase.
- The `v*exp(-|v|)` term is very specific and hard to replicate.

**Candidate 3:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c5 + c6*exp(c7*t) + c8*v³ + c9*cos(t)`
Set c0=0, c5=0, c6=0. Then: `c1*v + c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + c8*v³ + c9*cos(t)`. Set c3=1, c4=0, c9=0: `c1*v + c2*sin(t) + c8*v³`. This gives `v³ + v + sin(t)` terms but MISSING `v*exp(-|v|)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 7:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2 + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*exp(c6*v) + c7*v³ + c8*cos(t)`
Set c0=0, c2=0, c3=0. Then: `c1*v + c5*exp(c6*v) + c7*v³ + c8*cos(t)`. The `exp(c6*v)` term is NOT `v*exp(-|v|)`. Can't match. **No match.**

**Candidate 36:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2 + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*v³ + c6*cos(t) + c7*v*exp(c8*x)`
Set c0=0, c2=0, c3=0. Then: `c1*v + c5*v³ + c6*cos(t) + c7*v*exp(c8*x)`. The last term depends on x, not |v|. **No match.**

**Candidate 46:** `c0 + c1*v + c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*x^c5 + c6*v³ + c7*sin(c8*x + c9)`
Setting c2=0, c4=0: `c0 + c1*v + c6*v³ + c7*sin(c9)` — the sin becomes constant. Missing `v*exp(-|v|)` and `sin(t)`. **No match.**

Terms like `exp(c*v)` cannot replicate `v*exp(-|v|)` because of the absolute value and the multiplication by v.

Also, most candidates use `cos(t)` rather than `sin(t)`. While `sin(t)` and `cos(t)` are phase-shifted versions, a bare `cos(t)` with a coefficient cannot equal `sin(t)` for all t. Only candidates with `sin(c*t + c)` could handle this, but they still lack the `v*exp(-|v|)` term.

After checking all 50 candidates, none can reproduce the `v*exp(-|v|)` term from the GT.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO27)

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0585985712804097*v**3 - 0.716668620096812*v - 0.358334310048406*v*exp(-Abs(v)) + 0.66863216766915*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v**3` term
2. `v` term (linear)
3. `v*exp(-Abs(v))` term
4. `sin(t)` term

Note: There's NO `x` dependence, NO `exp(t)` dependence, and NO constant offset in the GT.

For any candidate to match, I need to be able to:
- Set coefficients of `x`-dependent terms to 0
- Set coefficients of `exp(t)` terms to 0
- Set any constant offset to 0
- Have `sin(t)` or equivalent (like `cos(t)` with phase shift — but `cos(t)` alone can't equal `sin(t)` unless combined with `sin(t)`)
- Have `v**3` term
- Have `v` term
- Have `v*exp(-Abs(v))` term — this is the critical, unusual term

Let me check: `cos(t)` ≠ `sin(t)`. We need `sin(t)`, which equals `cos(t - π/2)`. A standalone `cos(t)` with a free coefficient can match `sin(t)` only if we can shift the argument — but `cos(t)` has a fixed argument `t`, so `c*cos(t)` cannot equal `sin(t)`. However, `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2)`, and since the argument is fixed as `t` in `cos(t)`, we CANNOT make `cos(t) = sin(t)`.

Wait — but many candidates have `cos(t)`. Can `cos(t)` match `sin(t)`? No, `cos(t) ≠ sin(t)` for all t. So candidates with only `cos(t)` and no `sin(t)` cannot match the GT's `sin(t)` term.

Actually, let me reconsider. The GT has `sin(t)`. If a candidate has `c*cos(t)`, this cannot equal `sin(t)` — they are linearly independent. So candidates need `sin(t)` or `sin(c*t + c)` where the constants can be adjusted.

Now, the critical missing basis function in almost all candidates is `v*exp(-Abs(v))`. Let me scan for candidates that could produce this term.

Most candidates have terms like `v*x`, `v*x**2`, `exp(c*v)`, `exp(c*x)`, `log(...)`, etc. None of these can produce `v*exp(-Abs(v))`.

Let me check each candidate systematically for the `v*exp(-Abs(v))` term:

- Candidates with `exp(c*v)`: 7, 16, 22, 34, 37, 41, 44, 45, 47, 48 — these give `exp(c*v)`, not `v*exp(-|v|)`.
- Candidates with `v*exp(c*x)`: 36 — this is `v*exp(c*x)`, not `v*exp(-|v|)`.
- Candidates with `sin(c*v+...)`: 39 — `sin` of `v`, not `exp(-|v|)`.

None of the candidates contain `v*exp(-Abs(v))` or anything that can produce it. The term `v*exp(-|v|)` is a product of `v` and `exp(-|v|)`, which involves the absolute value function applied to `v`. Since `v` takes both signs, `|v|` cannot be simplified, and no candidate has this structure.

Even `exp(c*v)` cannot match `exp(-|v|)` because `exp(c*v)` is either `exp(cv)` for positive `v` or `exp(cv)` for negative `v`, while `exp(-|v|)` is `exp(-v)` for positive `v` and `exp(v)` for negative `v` — it's not a single exponential.

Since the `v*exp(-Abs(v))` term (with coefficient ≈ -0.358) is significant and cannot be produced by any candidate, **no candidate matches**.
